<div id="review_442446383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/442446383" />
    <a title="Bandit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4528663-bandit"><img alt="Bandit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289488158p2/4528663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/442446383?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bandit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bandit" href="/user/show/4528663-bandit">Bandit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423356981" href="/book/show/6202063-relentless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442446383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12866279729821428887">Dean Koontz writes of a marvelous world, world so simple, so incredibly black and white with absolutely nothing in between, world where you can tell an evil person from a mile away (hint, they actually look it), but it doesn't even matter cause good will always triumph over evil anyway, where characters start out one way or another (good or evil) and remain so for the rest of the book with no arc or character development whatsoever. Here are some sample cardboard characters...genius kid, uber su</span>
  <span id="freeText12866279729821428887" style="display:none">Dean Koontz writes of a marvelous world, world so simple, so incredibly black and white with absolutely nothing in between, world where you can tell an evil person from a mile away (hint, they actually look it), but it doesn't even matter cause good will always triumph over evil anyway, where characters start out one way or another (good or evil) and remain so for the rest of the book with no arc or character development whatsoever. Here are some sample cardboard characters...genius kid, uber supportive amazing gun toting wife, a lovable but barely capable protagonist, a canine companion so good that her farts don't smell (seriously, that's in the book), an evil looking demented psycho stalker with homicidal tendencies. The latter had to have been inspired by a negative review or several, so to err on the side of caution I'm being very generous with 3 stars here.<br />Overall though, the book works, it works in the way of a tepid tap water or a slice of wonderbread for a meal, it's serviceable, it's paced decently, I enjoyed the audio version's reader, he did fun character voices...it's ok, it's just not great by any means. It kept me company on several fitness walks. Koontz is a capable writer, but it doesn't really feel like he's trying to excel, just pass. He has his formula, his books sell, so he adheres to it. In a world of so many great or even pretty good books, I'm not sure why this would be someone's first choice, given options, but if you're just looking to mindlessly walk to it or something, it'll do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12866279729821428887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59419964" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/529087-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1193188887p2/529087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59419964?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/529087-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/529087-stephen?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/529087-stephen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59419964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15321809974252254812">I've been a fan of Dean Koontz for about 17 years now, and he is, by far, one of my favorite authors. I enjoyed reading 'Relentless', but I feel that something is missing that made me love his books. With the exception of the Odd Thomas novels, his last several books have been just quick fun reads, about a man or woman going up against an extremely evil person or group of people. I miss his longer novels like 'From the Corner of His Eye', 'By the Light of the Moon', 'Watchers' and my all time fa</span>
  <span id="freeText15321809974252254812" style="display:none">I've been a fan of Dean Koontz for about 17 years now, and he is, by far, one of my favorite authors. I enjoyed reading 'Relentless', but I feel that something is missing that made me love his books. With the exception of the Odd Thomas novels, his last several books have been just quick fun reads, about a man or woman going up against an extremely evil person or group of people. I miss his longer novels like 'From the Corner of His Eye', 'By the Light of the Moon', 'Watchers' and my all time favorite 'Lightning'. I have always loved the way that Koontz always leaves the reader with a sense of hope at the end of his books. Yet, still, I feel something is missing from his newer books that was there in his earlier novels and I can't quite put my finger on it yet. It's almost as if he has streamlined his own formula for writing a novel, or perhaps putting Koontz in a godlike status in my own pantheon of the writers i like, maybe i am expecting too much. Either way, I never want him to stop writing, as you can tell from this review i'm not the best writer so who am I to judge. All I can pass on is a feeling of something missing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15321809974252254812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2071827152" />
    <a title="Deb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5276322-deb"><img alt="Deb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526245087p2/5276322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2071827152?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/5276322-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781491516775" href="/book/show/20918691-relentless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2071827152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2122836458924964130"><i>
  <b>Relentless was… relentless.<br/></b>
</i><br/>First let me say that I normally do not read books by this author <i>Dean Koontz</i>. If it wasn’t for this being an audio book and I needing something to listen to during commuting and working hours… I probably would not have chosen this particular book in paper form for myself. <br/>However, having listened to it, it wasn’t that bad. Although, again I’m sure, that if this was anything other than audio, I may have put it down. In fact, I did have to rewind it towards the begi</span>
  <span id="freeText2122836458924964130" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Relentless was… relentless.<br /></b>
</i><br />First let me say that I normally do not read books by this author <i>Dean Koontz</i>. If it wasn’t for this being an audio book and I needing something to listen to during commuting and working hours… I probably would not have chosen this particular book in paper form for myself. <br />However, having listened to it, it wasn’t that bad. Although, again I’m sure, that if this was anything other than audio, I may have put it down. In fact, I did have to rewind it towards the beginning because I wasn’t sure that I comprehended what was said. I don’t blame the book, per se, this may have been my distraction. <br /> <br />What was this book was about? I guess I can say it’s a Relentless chase. I kept wondering why. Even having finished the book and being told the “why” or the why the author wanted us to know, I still ask why. Because to me it didn’t seem logical. This author may not deal in logic, so I will maybe listen to another book and have a judgement on that soon. Bottom line, some characters were being pursued. We don’t know technically why. It’s weird. When we get to the end… we still don’t know why. I felt like teleporting myself into the book and saying, “Wait, you were persuing these people cause why?” The reason felt like a waste of time. The reason made no sense. The reason felt like… “Aw, Man… come on Dean.. you’ve gotta give me a better reason.” I mean, all that running. All that killing. All that fear and drama and for what? I don’t even see the sense in that.” Even the classic fictional psychopath has a better reason than that.<br /> <br />So, I would like some avid <i>Dean Koontz</i> readers to tell me if this was one of his good ones? Or if this was a bad one even for him. Or maybe I just don’t get the <i>Koontz</i>formula. <br /> <br />I guess, I’m giving this a rating of 2. I guess I’ll give one more book a chance by this author before I write him off as just not my cup o’ tea. I don’t know about recommends. <br />Next.<br /><br /><i><b>UPDATE: </b><br />I wrote this review earlier in the day. After writing the review, I did attempt two other books by this author but I just could not get into them. It was taking too long to get into. I quit. He's not for me.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2122836458924964130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_63962015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63962015" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2532190-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63962015?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/2532190-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63962015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3314669958323218086">Simply, this is Koontz's best book to date. Granted, I'm in the "I just finished this book and I love it more than any book I've ever read" mentality, which usually subsides with time. But, that's how I feel right now about it.<br/>Koontz, unlike horror contemporary Stephen King, whose style really hasn't changed much in 35 years, has grown as a writer. Deadly serious in his prose early on, he's now added humor-- some of it subtle and black, of course, but also some of it hysterically obvious and alm</span>
  <span id="freeText3314669958323218086" style="display:none">Simply, this is Koontz's best book to date. Granted, I'm in the "I just finished this book and I love it more than any book I've ever read" mentality, which usually subsides with time. But, that's how I feel right now about it.<br />Koontz, unlike horror contemporary Stephen King, whose style really hasn't changed much in 35 years, has grown as a writer. Deadly serious in his prose early on, he's now added humor-- some of it subtle and black, of course, but also some of it hysterically obvious and almost slapstick-- to his thriller/horror stories. How he's able to mix both is incredible to me. But, now, as with RELENTLESS, his books make you laugh while you keep the light on all night to ward off the bogeyman. Sort of like if a roller coaster ride went through a Funhouse with a monitor at your seat showing Will Ferrell, Mel Brooks, and Woody Allen movies.<br />After the thrills, chills and humorous moments subside, though, you end up realizing what Koontz's point is in writing this book. Maybe most folks would pick up on it in the first few pages, but it took me to the very last paragraph to "get it." Without giving away the plot and events, Koontz is writing about the forces, some of them seemingly beyond our control, that try to dictate how you should live your life. It is about the restrictions some would like to place on our dreams, our ambitions, our loves, our passions, and, from an artist's point of view, the things he or she tries to express through whatever medium they use. In this case, it's an author's views as expressed through his characters and plot line in a book, but it's really about ALL art, and, ultimately, ALL of us.<br /><br />This is my favorite passage from "Relentless:"<br />'As long as I can remember, novelists and filmmakers and cult leaders have been depicting and predicting the end of the world by fire or ice, by asteroid or magnetic-pole shift, and they have always found a large audience for their visions.<br />In the hearts of modern men and women, there is an inescapable awareness that something is wrong with this slice of history they have inherited, that in spite of the towering cities and the might armies and the scinece-fiction techonology made real, the moment is fragile, the foundation undermined...<br />...But if disaster came, it would be the collapse of civilation, not the end of the world. This blue transparant sky, the sea, the shore, the land, the dark evergreens ever rising-- all would endure, unaffected by human misery...<br />...Fire, ice, asteroids and pole shifts are bogeymen with which we distract ourselves from the real threat of out time. In an age when everyone invents his own truth, there is no community, only factions. Without community, there can be no consensus to resist the greedy, the envious, the power-mad narcissists who seize control and turn the institutions of civilization into a series of doom machines.<br />Have a nice day.'<br /><br />And on that note, I conclude my review!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3314669958323218086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_571251755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571251755" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8221425-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442641949p2/8221425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571251755?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/8221425-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8221425-alex?shelf=intriguing-plot">intriguing-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8221425-alex?shelf=love-this-author">love-this-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8221425-alex?shelf=incredible-writing">incredible-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8221425-alex?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8221425-alex?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571251755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11967728645025410187">RELENTLESS (Pub. 2009) by Dean Koontz was a fascinating and great read. The author has a remarkably thoughtful way of bringing a thriller to life, and this is one of my favorite of his stories.<br/><br/>As a writer myself, I couldn't help but be caught up in the plot - a bestselling writer, Cubby Greenwich, is waylaid in a national book review by a famously viscious critic. Family and friends console Greenwich with words of praise and reminders of his success, but the horrid review still niggles. When Gre</span>
  <span id="freeText11967728645025410187" style="display:none">RELENTLESS (Pub. 2009) by Dean Koontz was a fascinating and great read. The author has a remarkably thoughtful way of bringing a thriller to life, and this is one of my favorite of his stories.<br /><br />As a writer myself, I couldn't help but be caught up in the plot - a bestselling writer, Cubby Greenwich, is waylaid in a national book review by a famously viscious critic. Family and friends console Greenwich with words of praise and reminders of his success, but the horrid review still niggles. When Greenwich finds out that the critic lives only twenty miles away from him, he can't resist having lunch at a restaurant the man is known to frequent. After an embarassing encounter in the restroom with the out-of-kilter critic, things begin to quickly unravel.<br /><br />The critic turns out to be a psychopath with an agenda, and immediately begins to make Greenwich sorry he'd ever met the man. As he and his family are forced to run for their lives from the killer critic, he learns that he is not the only author who has been threatened by this maniac. With no choice but to keep running, they flee town and try to regroup but the critic-killer is relentless. With help from friends and warnings from another author who's life has been destroyed by the maniac, Greenwich manages to stay one step ahead, but barely, right up until the end when it looks like they will all die a painful death.<br /><br />One of the things I enjoyed most about this story is the character of Greenwich's son Milo, who happens to be a six-yr-old physics prodigy. Koontz is known for using dog characters in his stories and who can resist a boy and his dog? A dog that can teletransport herself and lives to protect her young charge. It might take a bit of suspension of disbelief, but Koontz makes the ride so intriquing I had no problem with 'believing'.<br /><br />The visciousness of the killer, and the tangled plot will keep you turning pages right up to the last one. But the best thing about the story is Koontz remarkable ability to bring a thinking-man's depth to what could otherwise be just another great psyco thriller, and raises the bar without coming across as trying too hard. Koontz hits just the right notes with his descriptive passages and makes us care deeply about his well-spun characters. I couldn't put this book down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11967728645025410187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_482412547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482412547" />
    <a title="Bret" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2775605-bret"><img alt="Bret" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482412547?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bret" href="/user/show/2775605-bret">Bret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553591729" href="/book/show/7315605-relentless">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2775605-bret?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482412547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2386647453943835511">This has got to be one of the worst books I've ever read. Koontz continues to use the same plot and characters from most of his other books. Sure the names and the situation are different but it's the same general plot - someone finds themselves caught up in a situation that causes them to have to go on the run. In this instance, an author named Cubby Greenwich releases a new book that receives a bad review from book critic Shearman Waxx. After a run in with the critic in the bathroom of a resta</span>
  <span id="freeText2386647453943835511" style="display:none">This has got to be one of the worst books I've ever read. Koontz continues to use the same plot and characters from most of his other books. Sure the names and the situation are different but it's the same general plot - someone finds themselves caught up in a situation that causes them to have to go on the run. In this instance, an author named Cubby Greenwich releases a new book that receives a bad review from book critic Shearman Waxx. After a run in with the critic in the bathroom of a restaurant, the book critic begins to torment the author and his family causing them to go on the run.<br /><br />I didn't like a single character in this book. The main character/narrator, Cubby Greenwich, is just irritating. He's so good and wholesome but he's got something hidden in his past that no one knows about. Then there's the couples six year old son Milo, who is a super genius, already has his GED, and spends his time tinkering with and building electronic devices. I am so sick of reading books and watching movies with children who have high IQs. It's overdone and it's one of those things that just instantly annoys the crap out of me. <br /><br />There's also the family's dog who is always suddenly somewhere where she couldn't have possibly gotten to on her own. Oh, and the dog's portrayed as being above average intelligent too. How charming... So how does this dog keep ending up in places she shouldn't be? You have to wait til the last twenty pages to find out, although it's pretty obvious and you won't care by the time you do find out.<br /><br />Sherman Waxx has got to be one of the stupidest villains. Why is this critic trying to kill this author and his family? By the time the motive is told the reader could care less.<br /><br />Some sci-fi elements are thrown in at the last second to conveniently save a character from a bad fate, which I might add is alluded to at the end of at least five chapters.<br /><br />The book as a whole just feels absolutely ridiculous. The only reason I read it all the way through was because it was a quick book to read. I highly doubt I will take the time to read any of Dean Koontz's books that will be published after this one (that I haven't already bought).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2386647453943835511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160303272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160303272" />
    <a title="Chad Cantrell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4827318-chad-cantrell"><img alt="Chad Cantrell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295311337p2/4827318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160303272?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chad Cantrell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chad Cantrell" href="/user/show/4827318-chad-cantrell">Chad Cantrell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160303272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13654837502669603592">I think Koontz is to modern-day American novels what Hollywood is to modern-day American films. Flashy, over-the-top, and entertaining, but also very hit-or-miss, even from scene to scene. When I started <i>Relentless</i>, I honestly wasn't sure that I could finish it. Koontz tries so desperately to be funny and to show us how playful and carefree his three main characters are at the beginning of the novel that it's actually a little bit sad...and a lot annoying. (Seriously, does anyone find it funny t</span>
  <span id="freeText13654837502669603592" style="display:none">I think Koontz is to modern-day American novels what Hollywood is to modern-day American films. Flashy, over-the-top, and entertaining, but also very hit-or-miss, even from scene to scene. When I started <i>Relentless</i>, I honestly wasn't sure that I could finish it. Koontz tries so desperately to be funny and to show us how playful and carefree his three main characters are at the beginning of the novel that it's actually a little bit sad...and a lot annoying. (Seriously, does anyone find it funny that our hero thinks his feet are ugly?) If this had been written by anyone else, I probably would have taken it as a sign that the author was trying to make me emotionally attached to the characters before killing them off. With Koontz, however, there is never any sense of danger (nope, not even during gunfights, car chases, or explosions, and not even with Koontz repeatedly telling us that one of the characters is about to be shot). In all fairness, the book does get better as it progresses, but it requires that you read without questioning anything--the characters' motives, the seemingly limitless resources of the villain, the convenient little detail that always provides a means for narrow escape--and it would probably help to go ahead and abandon common sense, too, because the characters don't seem to have a lot of that. If you're a Koontz fan or just a little bored, you might have fun with this one, but I can't recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13654837502669603592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62269176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62269176" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2453991-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548801525p2/2453991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62269176?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/2453991-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62269176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12157498975024676553">I bought this book and literally couldn't wait to read it - HUGE Dean Koontz fan and this book sounded like it would follow along the lines of "Life Expectancy" which I adored. However, within the first chapter I began to realize that as much as I wanted to love this book and laugh out loud like I normally do, it wasn't going to happen. <br/><br/>This book almost seems like it's trying way too hard to be funny, whereas with Koontz's other books the humor was effortless. The amount of adjectives alone almo</span>
  <span id="freeText12157498975024676553" style="display:none">I bought this book and literally couldn't wait to read it - HUGE Dean Koontz fan and this book sounded like it would follow along the lines of "Life Expectancy" which I adored. However, within the first chapter I began to realize that as much as I wanted to love this book and laugh out loud like I normally do, it wasn't going to happen. <br /><br />This book almost seems like it's trying way too hard to be funny, whereas with Koontz's other books the humor was effortless. The amount of adjectives alone almost cause you to drown in over-wordage. Read the first two chapters of the book and you'll see immediately what I'm talking about. It's like he tried to make this a funny book with a slight suspense-thriller tinge, when it should have been the other way around - that's his winning recipe. The narration came off yappy and the descriptors were out of this world - in a sentence that had 12 words in it about 8 of them were adjectives. I read the book in one afternoon but I really had to push myself through the first several chapters - even considered returning the book! <br /><br />I hate that I didn't love it - it was just an "okay" book. I hope his next one is better but it seems like he is starting a streak of fluff books - "Your Heart Belongs to Me" and this one are duds in my estimation. <br /><br />Sorry Dean :o(</span>
  <a data-text-id="12157498975024676553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HTs0lAltXB8tsVjOclX/GZw1PFG0+YJG/5KZMlxsDQQdfEoqIU1/ut7FUQ7yH1fgQ8CBuTOnqyBviFKivm+k0A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S7NmFnLn2PJRpNrJu13Pj3EkAxRR0Q97pu3GeUQrF45L9BioWsf7V6LQ0wk7F2d2rtG+/NaPJh029w3ppii+Wg==')})
  }

Here a brilliant young man finds himself fighting <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5870624661006558200\" style=\"display:none\">From the #1 &quot;New York Times&quot; bestselling master of suspense comes a riveting thriller that probes the deepest terrors of the human psyche--and the ineffable mystery of what truly makes us who we are. Here a brilliant young man finds himself fighting for his very existence in a battle that starts with the most frightening words of all... At thirty-four, Internet entrepreneur Ryan Perry seemed to have the world in his pocket--until the first troubling symptoms appeared out of nowhere. Within days, he\'s diagnosed with incurable cardiomyopathy and finds himself on the waiting list for a heart transplant; it\'s his only hope, and it\'s dwindling fast. Ryan is about to lose it all...his health, his girlfriend Samantha, and his life. One year later, Ryan has never felt better. Business is good and he hopes to renew his relationship with Samantha.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/21899169-relentless">Quotes from Relentless</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I'm small, I'm young - and I'm so different. You've always respected that difference, and you've always trusted it. Trust me now. There's a reason I am the way I am, and there's a reason I was born to you. There's always a reason. We belong together.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;

          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Evil itself may be relentless. I will grant you that, but love is relentless too. Friendship is a relentless force. Family is a relentless force. Faith is relentless force. The human spirit is relentless, and the human heart outlasts - and can defeat - even the most relentless force of all, which is time.&rdquo;</span>
